### Key Applications

**5. Brainstorming**:
- **Rarely used** - "ä¸ªä½æ•°" (single-digit occurrences, line 459)
- Only when "æ²¡æœ‰å¤ªå¤šçš„çµæ„Ÿäº†" (line 459)

**6. Research Ideas**:
- **Self-generated from needs, NOT from literature** (line 464-471)
- AI cannot find valuable research gaps - too vague or too comprehensive
- Process: Need discovery â†’ Check if anyone did it â†’ Find gaps â†’ Improve

**7. Student Supervision** (Educator Control):
- Gives students **only simple execution tasks**: Copy code, run, record results (line 573-579)
- Provides complete instructions including how to modify
- Students become **monitors** of GPT output compliance, not thinkers
- **Deliberately prevents** student critical thinking: "åˆ»æ„çš„ä¸è®©ä»–å»åš creative thinking" (line 585)
- Assessment focus: **Engagement + semantic depth/breadth** (line 710-714)

**8. Student Assessment Tasks**:
- Assigns tasks **AI cannot do well**: Formulating research questions
- AI produces vague or overly-long questions - "ä¸€çœ¼å°±èƒ½çœ‹å‡ºæ¥" (immediately obvious, line 591-592)
- Students must independently narrow down research questions with value

**Tool Strategy**:
- **Claude Max $200/month**: Long code generation (1000+ lines)
- **GPT Team**: Simple tasks, web search
- **DeepSeek**: Chinese greetings/WeChat only (low trust for serious work)
- **Perplexity**: Early literature search (now replaced by GPT/Claude search)

**Capability Boundaries**:
- Line 342-343: Unfamiliar domains â†’ prone to errors
- Line 495-501: **Cannot help with model innovation** - must have explicit architecture specs
- Line 506-507: **No meta-cognition, no value judgment** - doesn't know what's worth doing
- Line 525-531: Can brainstorm and list info, but cannot determine value
- Line 639-645: Chain of thought not always optimal - can limit flexibility

**Student Problems**:
- Line 566-567: **Knowledge accumulation deficit**, not critical thinking deficit
- Need AI for rapid knowledge accumulation (foundational)
- Once foundation exists, can think critically through analogical transfer

## I026 - E-commerce Entrepreneur (Malaysia-Singapore)

**Background**: Solo entrepreneur, 27 years old, Life Science major, running E-commerce business between Malaysia and Singapore

### Core Pattern: High-Dependency Efficiency Optimization with Outsourced Verification

**Heavy AI Workflow Dependency** (line 36, 342):
- Line 36: **"I always started my workflow by AI"** - AI initiates every workflow
- Line 342: **"my decision making is really heavily dependent on AI"**
- Line 81: AI helps **70-80%** of work
- Line 354: Replaced friends/family consultation with AI - "now it's just me and the eye"

**Hierarchical Decomposition Request** (line 90):
- Line 90: **Multi-level breakdown** - "Even under the every single step, I will still ask the AI to help me generate even more detailed steps with that particular step"
- Systematic but **delegated** to AI, not self-decomposed

**Instagram Post Workflow** (line 66, 267-273):
- Line 66: Feeds AI photo info + **emotions to evoke** + information goals â†’ AI generates captions
- Line 267-273: AI output "too rigid" with em-dashes â†’ **Rewrites into personal story** instead of point-form
- Line 558-570: A/B testing different styles, observes audience reactions

**Trial-and-Error Approach** (line 96, 102):
- Line 96: "for me, it's more of the **trial and error**... not really a right and wrong answer"
- Line 102: **No cross-model verification** - "not really, because so far it's been quite okay"

**Friend-Outsourced Verification** (line 594):
- Line 594: **Copywriter friend reviews** posts and gives input
- Quality checking delegated to human expert

**Task-Differentiated Trust** (line 519-528, 246):
- Line 519-528: **100% trust for factual** ("How old is Singapore") vs **Low trust for sourcing** (needs own business connections)
- Line 246: **70% trust** overall, 30% for rephrasing tone
- Line 309: **NO AI for finance**

**AI Limitation Awareness** (line 132-138, 378, 600):
- Line 132-138: AI writing "too weak, sometimes a bit too rigid and too false" with **em-dash overuse**
- Line 378: "not really... still too rigid and not personal enough"
- Line 600: AI **cannot do "sensible" creative work yet** - optimization still needs humans

**Interview Preparation** (line 165, 180):
- Line 165: Uses AI for **interview roleplay** - feeds interviewer background + job description â†’ AI generates potential questions
- Line 165: "pretty accurate so far"

**Copyright Concerns** (line 453-486):
- Line 453-486: **Biggest fear**: Ideas shared with AI might leak to others - "all about the timing"
- Line 465: Keeps "most of the ideas to myself", only gives "non sensitive information"

**Efficiency Transformation** (line 348, 327):
- Line 348: Before AI: **Hours** researching viral posts â†’ After AI: **3 minutes** max with AI structure + tweaking
- Line 327: AI "really increased my efficiency... save manpower course"

### Key Applications

**1. Instagram Marketing Posts**:
- Process: Shoot photo â†’ Feed AI (photo content + emotions + info goals) â†’ AI generates caption â†’ Rewrite rigid parts into personal story

- After AI: 3 minutes (structure + tweaking)

- Result: "Pretty accurate so far"

- AI generates guideline + detailed workflow
- Then requests even MORE detailed sub-steps under each step
- Hierarchical decomposition approach

- AI finds brands producing specific footprint products
- Replaces physical supermarket checking
- Still needs own connections for final decisions

**5. Content Optimization**:
- AI provides 70% - structure, basic content
- Human adds 30% - personal tone, story elements, em-dash removal
- Friend copywriter reviews for final quality check

**Limitations Acknowledged**:
- AI writing too rigid, formal, em-dash heavy
- Cannot do "sensible" creative work with inspiration/vibe
- Not suitable for finance tasks
- Copyright concerns - keeps core ideas private

**Trust Calibration**:
- **100% trust**: Factual questions ("How old is Singapore?")
- **70% trust**: General marketing content (rephrases 30%)
- **Low trust**: Business partner sourcing (needs own connections)
- **Zero trust**: Finance tasks

**Efficiency Gains**:
- Marketing campaigns: Hours â†’ 3 minutes
- Manpower saved - solo operation viable
- Replaced consultation with friends/family

### Behavioral Signature

**"Reference-Conscious Pragmatist"** - é«˜ä¿¡ä»»ä½†éªŒè¯ä¸¥æ ¼å‹

**Core Characteristics**:
1. **Extreme Trust Growth**: 20-30% â†’ 90% (largest increase in recent cohort)

## I049 - Wee Chen Xian (Chemical Engineering Student)

**Background**: NTU Chemical Engineering undergraduate with second major in Business, working on process modeling project (Aspen Plus)

### High-Risk Scenarios
1. **Essay refinement/compression** (1000â†’300 words)
   - "I will copy paste **paragraph by paragraph**"
   - "summarize this paragraph, summarize that paragraph"
   - "if this doesn't work right, then I will go more in detail to **sentence**"
   - "**above 10 prompts**" per conversation

2. **Process modeling guidance** (Aspen Plus software)
   - "which column is most suitable?"
   - "we use that as a guidance for us to work on our result"
   - "we need to make it credible"

3. **Paraphrasing senior's work**
   - "we need to ask chat to help us to **paraphrase a bit**, right? So that we don't get detected **plagiarism**"
   - "it actually **remove the main points**"
   - "I have **Learned** that certain prompt is required... **paraphrase, but keep all the main points**"

### Low-Risk Scenarios
4. Technical explanations - "Generally you can explain pretty well... it is pretty good with all these technical case"
5. Simple calculations - though catches errors ("t is supposed to be 5")

### Subprocess Scores (based on high-risk scenarios)

| Subprocess | Score | Evidence | Rationale |
|------------|-------|----------|-----------|
| P1 Task Decomposition | 3 | âœ“âœ“âœ“ | "**paragraph by paragraph**" + "more in detail to **sentence**" + "merge two sentences into one" - Systematic hierarchical decomposition (essay â†’ paragraphs â†’ sentences) |
| P2 Goal Setting | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "I want **300 words**, reduce to 300 words" + "make it **flow smoother**, make it more **grammatically correct**" + "**keep all the important points**" - Clear task-specific goals |
| P3 Strategy Selection | 1 | âœ“ | Only ChatGPT mentioned, no tool comparison - Single tool |
| P4 Resource Planning | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "I will generate **my own ideas** and then I will throw into Ji" + "**list down what is my working**... Put it into chat GBT... use chat GBT as a **comparison**" - Some independent preparation |
| M1 Progress Monitoring | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "I'll **keep going back and forth** to produce most the in the draft" + "**above 10 prompts**" - Extended iteration tracking |
| M2 Quality Checking | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "I will **always need to check its work**" + "when I **check back**, then I'll from me, like, no, t is supposed to be 5" + "**do fact checking**" - Verification present |
| M3 Context Monitoring | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "by the **third prom**, right... it will start to be **less and less** already... I always need to **remind**... **send again the instruction**" - Aware of context drift patterns |
| E1 Result Evaluation | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "I realize that it can actually **solve more and more problems**" + "it can **generate better answer** compared to myself" - Clear evaluation criteria |
| E2 Learning Reflection | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "I have **Learned** that certain prompt is required. Like I need to **structure my prompt properly**" + "I come to realize that... 0 GBT that detects AI, right, is actually **pretty useless**" - Explicit experience-based learning |
| E3 Capability Judgment | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | "**technicalities**, right, usually it can do well" vs "I need to **prompt it better** to respond" + "the instruction that they give, right, if it's **not applicable** to my laptop" - Task-differentiated awareness |
| R1 Strategy Adjustment | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | Paragraph â†’ sentence when needed + "I **try to twist my words** and try to ask from a **different perspective**" + "I will **give up** and I will maybe start **searching on YouTube**" - Clear adjustment strategies |
| R2 Trust Calibration | 2 | âœ“âœ“ | Trust evolution: **10% â†’ 60-70%** + "use Stephanie to use GI as a **reference, not as the answer script itself**" + Technical tasks (high trust) vs accuracy (verification needed) - Task-differentiated trust with explicit boundaries |

**Total Score: 24/36**

### Pattern Determination

**PRIMARY PATTERN: C - Collaborative Co-Creation**

**Pattern C Indicators**:
- âœ… M1 â‰¥ 2 (actual: 2) - Extended iteration
- âœ… R1 â‰¥ 2 (actual: 2) - Adaptive strategy adjustment
- âœ… Total 18-26 (actual: 24) - Mid-range score
- âœ… Extended iteration count: "**above 10 prompts**"

**Mixed Pattern: C with A characteristics**
- **Pattern A trait**: Strong task decomposition (P1 = 3)
- **Pattern C dominance**: Extended iteration, comparison strategy, pragmatic trust

**Behavioral Signature**:
1. **Progressive decomposition**: Essay â†’ paragraphs â†’ sentences (similar to A)
2. **Extended iteration**: 10+ prompts per task (distinctive C trait)
3. **Context drift awareness**: "by the third prom... less and less" - monitors quality degradation
4. **Comparison strategy**: "list down my working... use chat GBT as a comparison"
5. **Pragmatic trust boundaries**: "use as reference, not as answer script"
6. **Adaptive abandonment**: Switches to YouTube when ChatGPT fails

**Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH** (clear C pattern with some A characteristics)

**Distinguishing from Pure Pattern A**:
- **Iteration style**: 10+ prompts (C) vs systematic verification (A)
- **Independence**: Some preparation (P4=2) vs independent-first (A requires P4â‰¥3)
- **Trust**: Pragmatic reference-based (C) vs systematic control (A)

**Key Difference from I001-I048 cohort**:
- **Context drift monitoring** (M3=2): Unique awareness that "by the third prompt" quality degrades
- **Hierarchical decomposition** (P1=3): Despite C pattern, shows A-level task breakdown
- **Explicit learning** (E2=2): "I have Learned that certain prompt is required"

### Key Quotes
- "I will copy paste **paragraph by paragraph**. I will say, okay, now summarize this paragraph, summarize that paragraph. And if this doesn't work right, then I will go more in detail to **sentence**."
- "I have **Learned** that certain prompt is required. Like I need to **structure my prompt properly**. I will need to say things like, okay, paraphrase, but **keep all the main points** in the paragraph."
- "by the **third prom**, right? I sent in the third paragraph, right? Then it will start to be **less and less** already. Meaning they paraphrase, less and less is more towards the original text that I sent in. So then I always need to **remind**, yeah, I always need to **send again the instruction**."
- "I will **list down what is my working**... Put it into chat GBT. And then I use chat GBT as a **comparison**. And yes, to see **who is actually correct**."
- "use Stephanie to use GI as a **reference, not as the answer script itself**, right? That... And definitely still need to go through **your own level of thinking**."
- "I realize that it can actually **solve more and more problems**. Then that's why my **reliance** on this AI tool becomes more and more."
- "I realize that **it can generate better answer compared to myself**. So it can produce a better result."

### Unique Characteristics

**Context Degradation Awareness**:
- **ONLY** interviewee to explicitly describe pattern: "by the third prom... less and less"
- Quantifies quality decay across prompts within single conversation
- Develops re-prompting strategy: "send again the instruction"

**Hierarchical Decomposition Strategy**:
- Essay â†’ Paragraphs â†’ Sentences
- Adaptive granularity: "if this doesn't work... more in detail"
- Similar to Pattern A but within iterative framework (Pattern C)

**Comparison-Based Trust**:
- "list down my working... use chat GBT as a comparison"
- Not independent-first (A) nor full delegation (B)
- Symmetric comparison: "see who is actually correct"

**Explicit Prompt Learning**:
- "I have Learned that certain prompt is required"
- "I need to structure my prompt properly"
- Evidence-based prompt refinement

**Pragmatic Abandonment**:
- "I will give up and I will maybe start searching on YouTube"
- Clear threshold for switching strategies
- Not all-or-nothing trust

**Trust Evolution Driver**:
- 10% â†’ 60-70% increase
- Driven by problem-solving success: "solve more and more problems"
- Output quality recognition: "generate better answer compared to myself"

**Academic Integrity Navigation**:
- Uses ChatGPT for paraphrasing senior's work to avoid plagiarism detection
- Learns to prompt: "paraphrase, but keep all the main points"
- Discovers AI detection tools unreliable: "turn it in detected at 0% AI. But... 0 GBT detected as 60%"

**Reliance Self-Awareness**:
- "more heavy reliance on chat DBT"
- "to certain extent, I have to agree" (can't live without it)
- But maintains boundaries: "use as reference, not as answer script"

### Domain Context
- **Academic**: NTU Chemical Engineering + Business
- **Project work**: Process modeling with Aspen Plus software
- **AI as enabler**: Uses ChatGPT to understand technical software features
- **Early adopter**: Started when ChatGPT "first launch" (GPT-3 era)
- **Usage intensity**: Daily, 10+ prompts per task
- **Self-efficacy**: High - feels "very equipped"

### Cross-Pattern Contrasts

**Highest Pattern A vs Highest Pattern D:**

| Aspect | I034 (Pattern A, 33/36) | I038 (Pattern D, 32/36) |
|--------|------------------------|------------------------|
| **Trust Evolution** | Constant 50% | Cycle: 20%â†’80%â†’20% |
| **Planning** | 12/12 PERFECT | 11/12 |
| **Regulation** | 5/6 | 6/6 PERFECT (ONLY) |
| **Approach** | Proactive control from start | Reactive evolution through experience |
| **Philosophy** | Epistemological rigor | Societal pattern recognition |
| **Stability** | "Never changed approach" | "Revert to old way of working" |
| **Knowledge Base** | Architecture understanding | AI field insider (paradoxically increases skepticism) |

**Highest Pattern C vs Lowest Pattern C:**

| Aspect | I019 (Pattern C, 33/36) | I014 (Pattern C, 16/36) |
|--------|------------------------|------------------------|
| **Context Adaptation** | Stakeholder framework | Binary importance filter |
| **Planning** | 12/12 PERFECT | 5/12 |
| **Monitoring** | 8/12 | 4/12 |
| **Verification** | Multi-AI validation | Zero (M2=0) |
| **Use Case** | Professional + Personal depth | Delegation only |

**Pattern B Range:**

| Aspect | I011 (Pattern B, 22/36) | I030 (Pattern B, 15/36) |
|--------|------------------------|------------------------|
| **Iteration** | 3-4è½® pragmatic | Delegates to team |
| **Learning** | Refuses investment (E2=1) | No reflection (E2=0) |

### Surprising Findings

1. **Pattern E Scarcity (2%)**: Only I006 explicitly builds prompt libraries
   - Expected: Learning orientation should be common
   - Reality: Most rely on ad-hoc strategies

2. **Undergraduate Exception (I038)**: 
   - Pattern D typically requires domain expertise
   - I038 (undergrad) achieves 32/36 through AI field education
   - Higher score than 85% of doctoral researchers

3. **Entrepreneur Paradox**:
   - I029 (non-technical, 23/36) > I030 (technical CEO, 15/36)
   - Personal iteration depth > delegation effectiveness

4. **Perfect Regulation Singularity**:
   - ONLY I038 achieves R1=R2=3 (6/6)
   - Pattern D signature: evolution-driven self-regulation
   - All Pattern A cases max at 5/6

5. **Context Drift Awareness**:
   - ONLY I049 explicitly describes quality degradation pattern
   - "by the third prompt... less and less"
   - Suggests most users unaware of context window effects

6. **AI Field Insider Effect**:
   - I013 (AI security research): High systematic control (33/36)
   - I038 (AI field student): High skepticism despite expertise
   - Technical knowledge â†’ divergent trust calibrations

### Metacognitive Maturity Indicators

**High Maturity (Score â‰¥30):**
- Explicit frameworks (I013å‘æ•£-æ”¶æ•›, I034 epistemological test)
- Multi-tool orchestration (I018 cherry-picking, I025 Claude Max)
- Self-regulation rules (I038 "as a rule", I020 "never trust")
- Quantified trust (I018 40-60% vs 80%+, I008 55å¼€ vs 91å¼€)

**Medium Maturity (Score 24-29):**
- Task decomposition without framework
- Verification present but unsystematic
- Tool selection based on experience
- Trust boundaries but not explicitly articulated

**Low Maturity (Score â‰¤20):**
- Reactive strategies only
- Minimal verification (often M2 â‰¤1)
- Single-tool reliance
- Binary or uncalibrated trust

### Recommendations for Future Research

1. **Investigate Pattern E scarcity**: Why don't more users build prompt libraries?
2. **Study I038's trust cycle**: Longitudinal analysis of expectation-disappointment patterns
3. **Examine context drift awareness**: Why only I049 notices quality degradation?
4. **Explore domain effects**: STEM vs Business metacognitive strategy differences
5. **Analyze entrepreneur delegation**: When does personal iteration outperform team delegation?
